المفاسد، ولذلك قال
(۱) وجود الله ليس كوجود الحوادث، لأن وجود الله ذاتي له أي ليس بتأثير مؤثر وفعل فاعل، ووجود الحوادث بتأثير الله وفعله لأنه تعالى كان وحده ولا شيء غيره كما ورد في الحديث الشريف كما رواه البخاري ومسلم وغيرهما، ثم أوجد جل جلاله الحوادث، فوجودها غير ذاتي لها بل هو طارئ عليها وعارض لها، ولكون وجوده تعالى ذاتيا لم يقبل سبحانه العدم في الأزل، ولا يقبله في الأبد والأزل هو استمرار الوجود في أزمنة مقدرة غير متناهية في جانب الماضي، ويقابله الأبد وهو استمرار الوجود في أزمنة مقدرة غير متناهية في جانب المستقبل، ويعبر عنه بما لا يزال (غ) بتصرف يسير، وأما غير الله تعالى فهي موجودات لها وجود غير وجود الله تعالى ، ولكنها ثابتة ومتحققة لتعلق فعل الله بها ، وفعله هو تعلق قدرته ، ولهذا قد يسمي البعض المخلوقات بأنها فعل الله ، ولا يريد أنها مجرد تعلق أو مجرد نسبة عدمية أو إشراقية ، بل يريد أن هذه المخلوقات الموجودة من متعلقات فعل الله فإذا انقطع تعلق قدرة الله تعالى ( أي فعله ( بها انعدمت المخلوقات فبقاؤها مشروط بدوام تعلق قدرة الله تعالى بها وليس فعل الله حالا بذاته والإلزم قيام الحوادث بذاته وغير ذلك العلامة الأمير في حاشيته على شرح عبد السلام على الجوهرة : " وأما غيره - أي غير الله - فهو فعله وذهب بعض المتصوفة والفلاسفة إلى أنه تعالى الوجود المطلق ، وأنَّ غيره لا يتصف بالوجود أصلاً حتى إذا قالوا : الإنسان موجود ، فمعناه أنَّ له تعلقاً بالوجود وهو الله تعالى، وهو كفر، ولا حلول ولا اتحاد . اهـ وهذه كلمة شريفة منه يبين فيها فساد مذهب وحدة الوجود وأنه مخالف لعقيدة أهل السنة ، ويزيد فيقول إن القائل بهذا المذهب لا يلزمه القول بالحلول والاتحاد ولذلك ترى بعض من يقول بوحدة الوجود ينفي الحلول والاتحاد مخادعاً للناس لأن كثيرا منهم يظن أن مذهب وحدة الوجود يلزمه القول بالحلول والاتحاد فهو يكتفي بنفي الحلول والاتحاد ليوهمهم أنه لا يخالف مذهب أهل ومن ينخدع به لا يعرف ما ذكرناه ، بل مذهب وحدة الوجود مبني على نفي تكثر الوجود وأما القول بالحلول والاتحاد فهما مبنيَّان على القول بتكثر الوجود، وإلا فلا حلول ولا اتحاد فتأمل. فيما ذكرناه هنا فهو مفيد جداً. (س) (۲) هذا الحديث رواه الحاكم في مستدركه بعدة أسانيد عن حذيفة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إن الله خالق كل صانع وصنعته". وقال : هذا حديث صحيح على شرط مسلم ولم يخرجاه.
٣٤
The first section: the essential attributes. They are called essential because describing by them indicates the essence itself without an additional meaning. (1) And it is a single attribute, which is existence. Existence is a necessary state for the essence as long as the essence is not caused by a cause. Accordingly, existence is an essential attribute, different in concept from the attributes of meanings and the negative attributes. For the attributes of meanings are existential attributes, the negative are non-existential, and the essential is a state; so it is a positive attribute that is not described by existence or non-existence. (1) There is disagreement about existence: whether it is identical to the existent or other. The position of Imam al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him, is the first, based on the denial of states (ahwal), and this is the relied-upon view because according to Imam al-Ash'ari there is no intermediary between existence and non-existence. So describing by it is a conceptual matter considered by the person, having no fixed reality. An example: if you take out a garment from a box, the garment is described as appearing, which is a conceptual matter, having no fixed reality in the external world such that it could be seen in itself; rather it is something the person considers. On this basis, calling existence an attribute according to the statement of some verifiers is not intended as the meaning subsisting in the thing, but rather that which is judged about it, whether it is identical to its reality, subsisting in it, or external to it. Thus this definition includes existence, the negative attributes, the attributes of meanings, and the attributes of meaning-status, even on the view denying states. The one who says that existence is conceptual is Imam al-Razi and others. Counting existence as an attribute on the Ash'ari view is based on the broader meaning of attribute, because it is said 'Allah exists', so existence is attributed to Allah, so existence is counted as an attribute on the Ash'ari school based on the broader meaning of attribute, which includes mere linguistic consideration, and that is intended here. As for Imam al-Razi, he says in some of his books that existence is conceptual in the sense that it is conceptual, not an attribute of meaning. This is based on his view that existence is additional to the essence mentally; so for him it is among the considerations that occur to essences mentally. So consideration here is not in the sense of the consideration attributed to Imam al-Ash'ari. This is the meaning of the homonymy of existence. Some ignorant people have been deluded that describing Allah with existence entails affirming true non-existence for creatures, mentioning that to support what they claim of the doctrine of the unity of existence (wahdat al-wujud) based on the idea that creatures, including this witnessed world, are mere considerations subsisting in the very essence of Allah. Some people refuted this by saying that if we affirm existence for creatures, then it would necessitate allowing Allah to share with others in an attribute. This claimant did not know that Imam al-Ash'ari denied this entailment by his statement of the homonymy of existence. This claimant would be forced to say that Allah has nothing in His kingdom that has existence, and that is contrary to the fact that Allah is the Creator, which is certain. (S) al-'Allama al-Bayjuri said: Know that as some have said, it is not obligatory upon the legally responsible person to believe any of that; rather it suffices that he believe that Allah exists, even if he does not believe that existence is identical to the existent or other, because this is something about which the theologians have differed at length. So memorize that. (J). Tahdhib Sharh al-Sanusiyyah (1) It is not described by existence or non-existence. Then it is a state of the essence, not of the attributes, with the permissibility of saying, for example, 'Allah's power exists', and likewise His will and His knowledge, up to the rest of the attributes of meanings. And the attribute of existence is also necessary for the essence as long as the essence—i.e., the attribute—is not caused by a cause. This is unlike the states of meaning-status, such as His being willing and His being powerful, for these are caused by the meanings. The meaning of causation here is the conjunction in that the cause gives its effect existence. The proof for the existence of Allah from the Book is His saying, 'Allah is the Creator of everything' (az-Zumar 62). And from the Sunnah is his saying, 'Indeed Allah is the Maker of every maker and his handiwork.' And the ummah has unanimously agreed that Allah exists. As for the rational proof, it will come later. Among the corruptions, therefore he said: (1) The existence of Allah is not like the existence of contingent things, because the existence of Allah is essential to Him, i.e., not by the effect of an influence or the act of an agent. The existence of contingent things is by the effect of Allah and His act, because He was alone and nothing else with Him, as mentioned in the noble hadith narrated by al-Bukhari, Muslim, and others. Then He brought contingent things into existence, so their existence is not essential to them, rather it is accidental and incidental to them. Because His existence is essential, He does not admit non-existence in pre-eternity, nor does He admit it in post-eternity. Pre-eternity (azal) is the continuation of existence in assumed times infinite in the past direction; its opposite is post-eternity (abad), which is the continuation of existence in assumed times infinite in the future direction, and it is expressed by 'what is not yet' (ma la yazal). As for other than Allah, they are existents having existence other than Allah's existence, but they are fixed and realized due to the attachment of Allah's act to them, and His act is the attachment of His power. For this reason, some may call creatures 'the act of Allah', not intending that they are mere attachment or a non-existential or illuminative relation, but intending that these created existents are among the things to which Allah's act is attached. If the attachment of Allah's power (i.e., His act) to them were cut off, the creatures would cease to exist. So their continuance is conditioned by the permanence of the attachment of Allah's power to them. And Allah's act is not a state subsisting in His essence, for that would entail contingent accidents subsisting in His essence, etc. al-'Allama al-Amir said in his gloss on Sharh 'Abd al-Salam on al-Jawhara: 'As for other than Him—i.e., other than Allah—it is His act. Some of the Sufis and philosophers went to the view that He is absolute existence, and that other than Him is not described with existence at all, so when they say 'man exists', its meaning is that he has an attachment to existence, which is Allah. This is disbelief, and it does not entail indwelling (hulul) or union (ittihad).' This is a noble statement from him in which he shows the corruption of the doctrine of the unity of existence (wahdat al-wujud) and that it contradicts the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah. He adds that the adherent of this doctrine is not necessarily led to say indwelling or union. Therefore you see some who say the unity of existence deny indwelling and union, deceiving people, because many of them think that the doctrine of the unity of existence necessarily entails indwelling and union. So he suffices with denying indwelling and union to make them think that he does not contradict the school of Ahl al-Sunnah. Whoever is deceived by him does not know what we have mentioned. Rather, the doctrine of the unity of existence is based on denying the multiplicity of existence. As for the statement of indwelling and union, they are based on affirming the multiplicity of existence. Otherwise, there is no indwelling and no union. So reflect on what we have mentioned here, for it is very beneficial. (S) (2) This hadith was narrated by al-Hakim in his Mustadrak through multiple chains from Hudhayfa who said: The Messenger of Allah said, 'Indeed Allah is the Creator of every maker and his handiwork.' He said: This hadith is sahih according to the condition of Muslim, but they did not record it. 34
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the attribute of existence (al-wujud) as one of the essential attributes (al-sifat al-nafsiyyah) in Ash'ari theology, also discussing the disagreement about its nature and refuting the doctrine of the unity of existence (wahdat al-wujud). The author begins by defining al-sifat al-nafsiyyah: they are attributes that indicate the essence itself without any additional meaning. Then he states that there is only one such attribute: existence. Existence is defined as a necessary state (hal wajibah) for the essence as long as the essence is not caused by a cause (ghayr mu'allalah bi-'illah). This means existence is not an accident or a quality added to the essence; it is the essence itself in a certain state. The author then explains that existence is conceptually different from the attributes of meanings (ma'ani) and the negative attributes (salbiyyah). The attributes of meanings are existential qualities like knowledge and power; negative attributes are non-existential like not being a body; the essential attribute is a state (hal) that is positive (thubutiyyah) but not described by existence or non-existence itself. A long footnote clarifies the disagreement over whether existence is identical to the existent ('ayn al-mawjud) or other. Imam al-Ash'ari holds the first view, based on the denial of states (ahwal) — there is no intermediary between existence and non-existence, so the description 'existent' is a conceptual matter (i'tibari) that the mind applies, not a real attribute subsisting in the thing. The author gives the example of a garment's appearance when taken out of a box. Imam al-Razi considers existence conceptual in a different sense: it is mentally added to the essence. The Ash'ari counting of existence as an attribute is based on the broader meaning of attribute (al-ma'na al-a'mm), which includes any judgment about the thing, whether identical to its essence or not. The author warns against a dangerous misunderstanding: some ignorant people think that affirming existence for Allah and creatures on the same shared meaning would lead to affirming real non-existence for creatures (since if existence is one, then creatures must be non-existent). This is used to support the heretical doctrine of wahdat al-wujud (unity of existence), which holds that only Allah truly exists and creatures are mere considerations. The Ash'ari response is that existence is homonymous (mushtarak lafzi) for Allah and creatures, so no such entailment occurs. The author then resumes the main text, stating that existence is a state of the essence, not of the attributes, but we can speak of the existence of attributes like power. Existence is necessary for the essence and not caused, unlike the states of meaning-status (ahwal ma'nawiyyah) such as being willing, which are caused by the attributes of meaning. The text then provides proofs for Allah's existence: from the Quran (az-Zumar 62), from the Sunnah (the hadith 'Allah is the Maker of every maker'), and from Ijma' of the ummah. A rational proof is promised later. Another part of the footnote explains that Allah's existence is not like that of contingent things: His existence is essential (dhati), not caused, while creatures' existence is contingent and dependent on His act. The terms azal (pre-eternity) and abad (post-eternity) are defined. Creatures' continuance depends on the continuous attachment of Allah's power. The author concludes with a strong refutation of wahdat al-wujud, citing al-Amir: it is disbelief, and it is not the same as hulul or ittihad. The refutation clarifies that wahdat al-wujud denies multiplicity of existence, while hulul and ittihad affirm multiplicity; the two are distinct, and the proponents of wahdat al-wujud often deny hulul and ittihad to deceive others into thinking they are not deviant.

Key Terms
الوجود
الأزل
الأبد
وحدة الوجود
الحلول
الاتحاد
فعل الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that only Allah truly exists and creatures are mere illusions/considerations (wahdat al-wujud).
Correction: This is kufr. Creatures have real existence, though it is contingent and dependent on Allah's act. The term 'existence' is homonymous for Allah and creatures.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of the doctrine of wahdat al-wujud?
A) It is a valid Sufi interpretation
B) It is disbelief (kufr)
C) It is the same as hulul and ittihad
D) It is a minority but acceptable opinion

Key Takeaway
Allah's existence is essential and unique; creatures exist really but contingently; the doctrine of wahdat al-wujud is kufr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
You affirm that Allah alone is the Creator, but does your heart associate any creature with that power? Are there things you fear or love as if they had independent influence? Confess one such inclination now and resolve to direct all reliance to Allah alone.

Definition and Enumeration of Negative Attributes
Sanusi defines negative attributes and lists five.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of negative attributes in Islamic theology and be able to list the five negative attributes of Allah.

Core Idea
Negative attributes negate imperfections from Allah, affirming His transcendence.

Sanusi now introduces the second category of divine attributes: the negative attributes. These attributes do not describe what Allah is, but what He is not — they negate any imperfection or limitation. Understanding them is essential for tawhid. This passage defines them and lists the five foundational ones.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. Notice the structure: first a definition, then an explanation of the name, then the list.
The footnote marker (1) is likely a reference; ignore it for now.
2
Understand the significance of the name

The phrase 'most important of mothers' emphasizes their foundational role.
3
Memorize the five attributes
The passage lists five specific attributes. Commit them to memory: qidam, baqa', mukhalafa, qiyam binafsih, wahdaniyya. Understand the basic meaning of each.
These five are the core negative attributes in Ash'ari theology.

These attributes are essential for affirming Allah's transcendence.

The Attribute of Qidam: Definition and Key Distinctions
Author defines qidam, discusses permissibility of the name, and distinguishes it from azali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of qidam as the negation of prior non-existence, the rational permissibility of calling Allah 'qadim', and the important distinction between 'qadim' and 'azali'.

Core Idea
Allah's pre-eternity means His existence was never preceded by non-existence.

In this passage, the author establishes the attribute of qidam (pre-eternity) as fundamental to Islamic theology. He first defines it clearly, then addresses a controversy over applying the term 'qadim' to Allah, and finally distinguishes it from the related concept of 'azali'. These distinctions are crucial for avoiding misconceptions about the nature of divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of qidam
Start with the opening line where qidam is defined as 'negation of prior non-existence'. Understand that this means Allah's existence was never preceded by non-existence.
Notice the precise wording: 'intifa al-adam al-sabiq lil-wujud'.
2
Explore the permissibility of the name 'Qadim'
Examine the arguments for calling Allah 'qadim': consensus and a hadith. Note the refutation of those who forbid it, especially anthropomorphists.
The hadith from Abu Dawud is cited as evidence.
3
Understand the distinction between 'Qadim' and 'Azali'
Al-Sa'd explains that 'azali' is more general than 'qadim'. 'Qadim' applies only to what subsists by itself with no beginning, while 'azali' applies to both essence and attributes.
Attributes are called 'azali' but not 'qadim' according to some.
4
Compare the views of early Ash'aris and Mu'tazila
Note that early Ash'aris said attributes are azali but not qadim, while Mu'tazila deny that Allah can be described as qadim at all. The author promises a later refutation.
This shows the importance of precise theological language.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أولا : القدم (٢): وحقيقة القدم (۳) عبارة عن انتفاء العدم السابق للوجود، بمعنى أن وجود الله تعالى لم يسبقه العدم. (۲) الصحيح أنه يجوز إطلاق القديم عليه تعالى لثبوت ذلك بالإجماع ووروده في بعض الروايات بدل الأول (ج) قلت : الصحيح أنه يجوز ذلك مطلقاً أما الإجماع فهو من أهل السنة وسائر الفرق المعتبرة خلافاً لمن منع ذلك من المجسمة من أتباع ابن تيمية وابن قيم الجوزية، وأن معناه نفس معنى "الأول"، كما وضحناه أعلاه، وقد ورد في بعض الأخبار الحسنة أو الصحيحة قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : "أعوذ بالله العظيم وبوجهه الكريم وسلطانه القديم من الشيطان الرجيم ... " فوصف السلطان بأنه قديم. فيجوز نسبته إليه تعالى، وهذا الحديث حسن أو صحيح كما مر، رواه أبو داود عن عبدالله بن عمرو بن العاص عن النبي . والحديث الذي أشار إليه العلامة البيجوري رواه ابن ماجه عن أبي هريرة وهو ضعيف، وما ذكرناه أقوى في الدلالة على الجواز والمسألة أي إطلاق اسم عليه تعالى ظنية تكفي فيها الأدلة الظنية لأنها من باب العمليات لا الاعتقادات، بخلاف الكلام في معنى القديم كما هو بين للفطن (س). (۳) قال السعد : الأزلي أعم من القديم إذ القديم ما قام بنفسه ولا أول لوجوده، والأزلي ما لا أول له عدمياً كان أو وجودياً قائماً بنفسه أو بالذات العلية، فصفات الله يقال لها أزلية ولا يقال لها قديمة، وأما ذات الله فهي أزلية قديمة (ص). وقال شارح الإحياء : وقال عبدالله بن سعيد وأبو العباس القلانسي وهما من قدماء الأشاعرة أن القديم بمعنى يقوم به فهم يقولون أن الإله سبحانه قديم لمعنى قديم قائم به، ويقولون أن صفاته قائمة به موجودة أزلية ولا يقال إنها قديمة ولا محدثة وزعمت المعتزلة أن الله تعالى لا يوصف بأنه قديم ولا بأنه كان عالماً في الأزل بنفسه، وسيأتي البحث في ذلك والرد عليهم إن شاء الله .(الزبيدي).
First: Pre-eternity (al-qidam) (2): The reality of qidam (3) is the negation of prior non-existence to existence, meaning that the existence of Allah, exalted, was not preceded by non-existence. (2) The correct view is that it is permissible to apply the term 'qadim' (ancient) to Him, exalted, because it is established by consensus and appears in some narrations instead of 'al-awwal' (the First). (I say: The correct view is that it is absolutely permissible. As for consensus, it is from Ahl al-Sunna and all considered groups, contrary to those who forbid it from the anthropomorphists (mujassima), followers of Ibn Taymiyya and Ibn Qayyim al-Jawziyya, and its meaning is the same as 'al-awwal', as we clarified above. It has come in some good or authentic traditions: the Prophet, peace be upon him, said, 'I seek refuge with Allah the Great, and with His Noble Face, and His Ancient Authority (sultanihi al-qadim) from the accursed Satan...' So authority is described as 'qadim'. So it is permissible to attribute it to Him, exalted. This hadith is good or authentic as above, narrated by Abu Dawud from ‘Abdullah b. ‘Amr b. al-‘As from the Prophet. The hadith to which al-‘Allama al-Bayjuri referred is narrated by Ibn Majah from Abu Hurayra and is weak. What we mentioned is stronger in indicating permissibility, and the matter of applying a name to Him, exalted, is speculative; speculative evidence suffices because it is from the domain of actions, not beliefs, unlike the discussion about the meaning of qadim, as is clear to the intelligent. (S). (3) Al-Sa’d said: 'al-Azali' is more general than 'al-qadim', because al-qadim is that which subsists by itself and has no beginning to its existence, while al-azali is that which has no beginning, whether non-existent or existent, subsisting by itself or by the High Essence. So the attributes of Allah are called 'azaliyya' and not 'qadima', while the essence of Allah is both azali and qadim. (S). And the commentator of al-Ihya’ said: ‘Abdullah b. Sa’id and Abu al-‘Abbas al-Qalanisi, who are among the early Ash‘aris, said that al-qadim means that which subsists by itself. They say that God, glorified, is qadim by a qadim meaning subsisting in Him, and they say that His attributes subsist in Him, are existent, and azali, but they are not called qadima nor created. The Mu‘tazila claimed that Allah, exalted, is not described as qadim nor as having been knowing in pre-eternity by Himself, and the research on that and the refutation of them will come, Allah willing. (al-Zabidi).
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage examines the attribute of al-qidam (pre-eternity). It first defines it as the negation of prior non-existence. Then two footnotes elaborate. The first footnote (2) argues for the permissibility of calling Allah 'qadim', citing consensus and a hadith from Abu Dawud. It refutes those who forbid it, especially anthropomorphists. The second footnote (3) distinguishes between 'qadim' and 'azali': 'qadim' applies only to what subsists by itself with no beginning, while 'azali' is more general, applying also to attributes. Early Ash‘aris considered attributes 'azali' but not 'qadim'. The passage also mentions the Mu‘tazila position that Allah is not described as qadim, promising a later refutation.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'qadim' and 'azali' are synonymous and can be used interchangeably for both essence and attributes.
Correction: The passage clarifies that 'azali' is more general: it applies to anything without a beginning, including attributes. 'Qadim' specifically applies to what subsists by itself, i.e., the divine essence. Thus, attributes are called 'azali' but not 'qadim'.

Key Takeaway

The Attribute of Pre-Eternity: Definition and Three Types
Defines the attribute of pre-eternity and divides it into three types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of divine pre-eternity (al-qidam) and why only essential pre-eternity applies to Allah.

Core Idea
True pre-eternity is absolute beginninglessness—only Allah possesses it.

This lesson introduces the first negative attribute: pre-eternity. The author defines it as the negation of prior non-existence and then distinguishes three types. By understanding this distinction, you will see why Allah's pre-eternity is unique and cannot be compared to temporal or relative pre-eternity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once aloud or silently. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own definitions and divisions sink in before you analyze them.
2
Identify the definition and three types
Find where the author defines pre-eternity and then lists its three divisions. Notice the examples given for each type: essential, temporal, and relative.
Essential pre-eternity is for Allah; temporal and relative are given as contrasts.
3
Understand why temporal and relative are impossible for Allah
The author gives a brief argument: claiming Allah is temporally pre-eternal leads to absurd consequences. Read that part again and reflect on why each consequence is false.
This solidifies the doctrine that Allah's pre-eternity is absolute, not relative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأولا : القدم. وحقيقة القدم عبارة عن انتفاء العدم السابق للوجود، بمعنى أن وجود الله تعالى لم يسبقه العدم. والقدم مطلقاً ثلاثة أقسام؛ قِدَمُ ذات وقدمُ زمان وقدم إضافي. فالقدم الذاتي قدم الله تعالى أي قدم ذاته وصفاته، والزماني كقدم أمس على اليوم، والإضافي كقدم الأبوة على البنوة. فالزماني والإضافي مستحيلان على الله تعالى. فلو قلت إن الله قديم بالزمان، للزمك طروء الحوادث عليه، وقدم الزمان قطعا وجواز التسلسل في القدم، وكل هذا باطل.
And first: pre-eternity (al-qidam). And the reality of pre-eternity is an expression of the negation of prior non-existence to existence, meaning that the existence of Allah, the Exalted, was not preceded by non-existence. And pre-eternity absolutely is of three divisions: essential pre-eternity, temporal pre-eternity, and relative pre-eternity. Essential pre-eternity is the pre-eternity of Allah, the Exalted, i.e., the pre-eternity of His essence and attributes. Temporal pre-eternity is like the pre-eternity of yesterday relative to today. Relative pre-eternity is like the pre-eternity of fatherhood relative to sonship. Temporal and relative pre-eternity are impossible for Allah, the Exalted. So if you say that Allah is pre-eternal in time, then there would necessarily follow for you the occurrence of originated events upon Him, and the pre-eternity of time absolutely, and the permissibility of an infinite regress in pre-eternity, and all of this is false.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage classifies the first negative attribute, pre-eternity (القدم). It begins with a definition: pre-eternity is the negation of prior non-existence, meaning that Allah's existence was never preceded by non-existence. Then it divides pre-eternity into three types: essential pre-eternity (قدم ذات), temporal pre-eternity (قدم زمان), and relative pre-eternity (قدم إضافي). Essential pre-eternity belongs to Allah's essence and attributes; it is absolute beginninglessness. Temporal pre-eternity is a relative comparison, like yesterday being older than today, and relative pre-eternity is a relational priority, like fatherhood being prior to sonship. The passage then argues that both temporal and relative pre-eternity are impossible for Allah because they would imply that Allah is subject to time, which involves change and originated events (حوادث). If one claimed that Allah is pre-eternal in time, it would entail that originated events occur in Him, that time itself is pre-eternal, and that an infinite regress of pre-eternities is possible—all of which are false. Thus, only essential pre-eternity is affirmed for Allah.

Key Terms
القدم
قِدَمُ ذات
قدم زمان
قدم إضافي
انتفاء العدم السابق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Confusing temporal pre-eternity (قدم زمان) with essential pre-eternity, thinking that Allah's pre-eternity involves time.
Correction: Temporal pre-eternity implies a relationship with time, which necessarily involves change and originated events. Allah is beyond time; His pre-eternity is absolute and not relative to any temporal measure.

Checkpoint
Which type of pre-eternity is attributable to Allah according to this passage?
A) Temporal pre-eternity
B) Relative pre-eternity
C) Essential pre-eternity
D) All three

Key Takeaway
Only essential pre-eternity — absolute beginninglessness — is attributable to Allah, while temporal and relative pre-eternity are impossible for Him.

The Three Types of Qidam and the Proofs for Allah's Essential Eternity
Defines Qidam, divides into three types, provides scriptural proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three divisions of Qidam (pre-existence) and why only essential pre-existence applies to Allah, supported by scriptural proofs.

Core Idea
Only essential pre-existence befits Allah; temporal and relative pre-existence are impossible for Him.

This passage from Sanusi’s foundational text classifies the attribute of pre-existence (qidam) into three distinct types. Before we can properly affirm that Allah is eternal, we must differentiate between eternity inherent to His essence, eternity measured by time, and eternity that is merely relative. The author then provides decisive scriptural evidence from the Qur'an, the Prophet’s own words, and the consensus of the Muslim community.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic source passage slowly, then read the English translation. Notice the technical terms: قدم ذات, قدم زمان, قدم إضافي.
The passage is concise; each division is defined by an example.
2
Identify the three divisions and their definitions
The passage lists three types of qidam. Find how each is defined and what example is given. Observe that the author says 'absolutely (mutlaqan)' to indicate the general classification.
Essential pre-existence is the only one affirmed for Allah.
3
Understand why temporal and relative pre-existence are impossible for Allah
The author explains that claiming Allah is eternal in time (temporal) leads to problematic consequences: occurrence of events upon Him, pre-existence of time itself, and infinite regress. These are all false, so only essential pre-existence remains.
This is a key point: qadim bil-zaman is not what we mean by 'Allah is eternal.'
4
Review the scriptural proofs and the consensus
The passage gives the Qur'anic verse 'He is the First' (57:3), the hadith 'O Allah, You are the First, so there is nothing before You,' and the consensus (ijma') that Allah is described with essential pre-existence. Check that each proof directly supports the attribute.
The rational proof is promised later; here only transmitted proofs are given.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقدم مطلقاً ثلاثة أقسام: قدم ذات وقدم زمان وقدم إضافي. فالقدم الذاتي قدم الله تعالى أي قدم ذاته وصفاته، والزماني كقدم أمس على اليوم، والإضافي كقدم الأبوة على البنوة. فالزماني والإضافي مستحيلان على الله تعالى. فلو قلت إن الله قديم بالزمان، للزمك طروء الحوادث عليه، وقدم الزمان قطعا وجواز التسلسل في القدم، وكل هذا باطل. والدليل على أن الله تعالى متصف بالقدم من الكتاب قوله تعالى ﴿ هُوَ الْأَوَّلُ ﴾ الحديد، ومن السنة قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "اللهم أنت الأول فليس قبلك شيء". وقد أجمعت الأمة على أن الله تعالى متصف بالقدم، فلم يسبق ذاته ولا صفاته عدم. وأما برهان العقل فسيأتي.
And pre-existence (qidam) absolutely is three divisions: essential pre-existence (qidam dhat), temporal pre-existence (qidam zaman), and relative pre-existence (qidam idafi). Essential pre-existence is the pre-existence of Allah Most High, meaning the pre-existence of His essence and attributes. Temporal pre-existence is like the pre-existence of yesterday relative to today. Relative pre-existence is like the pre-existence of fatherhood relative to sonship. Temporal and relative pre-existence are impossible for Allah Most High. Thus, if you say that Allah is eternal in time (qadim bil-zaman), there would necessarily follow for you the occurrence of events upon Him, the absolute pre-existence of time, and the possibility of regress in pre-existence—all of this is false. The proof that Allah Most High is described with pre-existence from the Book is His saying: "He is the First" (al-Hadid). From the Sunnah is his saying, peace and blessings be upon him: "O Allah, You are the First, so there is nothing before You." And the community has unanimously agreed that Allah Most High is described with pre-existence (al-qidam), so neither His essence nor His attributes were preceded by non-existence. As for the rational proof, it will come later.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage defines and classifies the attribute of Qidam (eternity/pre-existence). It begins by stating that qidam in an absolute sense is of three divisions: essential (qidam dhat), temporal (qidam zaman), and relative (qidam idafi). Essential pre-existence is the pre-existence of Allah's essence and attributes—this is the only type befitting Him. Temporal pre-existence is like the pre-existence of yesterday over today; relative pre-existence is like the pre-existence of fatherhood over sonship. Both temporal and relative pre-existence are impossible for Allah because they entail succession of events, the pre-existence of time itself, and the possibility of an infinite regress—all of which are false. The author then provides proofs from the Qur'an ('He is the First') and the Sunnah (the hadith 'O Allah, You are the First, so there is nothing before You'), followed by citing the consensus (ijma') of the Muslim community that Allah is described with essential eternity, meaning that neither His essence nor attributes were ever preceded by non-existence. The rational proof is deferred to a later discussion.

Key Terms
قدم
ذات
زمان
إضافي
أول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Qidam means Allah is eternal in time (temporal pre-existence).
Correction: The correct doctrine is essential pre-existence, which negates any temporal succession or relation to time.

Checkpoint
How many divisions of Qidam (pre-existence) does the author mention, and which one applies to Allah?
A) Two divisions; essential and temporal; Allah has temporal pre-existence.
B) Three divisions; essential, temporal, and relative; Allah has essential pre-existence.
C) Three divisions; essential, temporal, and relative; Allah has temporal pre-existence.
D) One division; essential only; Allah has essential pre-existence.

Key Takeaway
Allah alone has essential pre-existence; temporal and relative pre-existence are impossible for Him, as proven by Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe Allah is the First, with nothing before Him. But do you live as if something in your life—your career, your relationships, your worries—came before Him in your heart? What would it take to truly place Him first today?
?
The passage teaches that time is a created measure and cannot apply to Allah. Have you ever imagined Allah as existing 'within' time? What does it mean for your worship to know that Allah is beyond the timeline of your past, present, and future?
?
If essential pre-existence belongs only to Allah, then everything else is contingent and began. Does your soul acknowledge its total dependence on the First, or do you secretly feel self-sufficient? What area of your life are you most likely to act as if you are the 'first' cause?

The Attribute of Priority (al-Awwaliyya) in the Prophet's Supplication
Presents a prophetic supplication containing the attribute 'al-Awwal'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's supplication using 'al-Awwal' (the First) provides evidence for the attribute of absolute priority, which is essentially the same as 'qadim' in meaning.

Core Idea
The attribute 'al-Awwal' in the hadith establishes Allah's absolute priority over all creation.

This lesson examines a well-known supplication of the Prophet that includes the description 'You are the First, so there is nothing before You.' This phrase explicitly affirms that Allah has no beginning, which is the core meaning of 'qadim'. The lesson presents the transmission of this hadith from multiple sources.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith text
Read the Arabic supplication carefully and note the phrase 'anta al-awwalu fa laysa qablaka shay'. Then read the translation.
2
Identify the key attribute
Notice that 'al-Awwal' is used here as a description of Allah. Reflect on its meaning: the One who exists before everything else.
3
Consider the chain of transmission
The hadith is narrated by Bukhari, Tirmidhi, and others. The strong chain adds to its reliability as evidence.
4
Connect to 'Qadim'
Understand that scholars use 'qadim' to refer to the same concept of pre-eternity. This hadith provides a scriptural basis for the attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
روى هذا الحديث البخاري في الأدب المفرد عن أبي هريرة قال : " كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : إذا أوى إلى فراشه اللهم رب السماوات والأرض ورب كل شيء فالق الحب والنوى منزل التوراة والإنجيل والقرآن أعوذ بك من كل ذي شر أنت آخذ بناصيته أنت الأول فليس قبلك شيء وأنت الآخر فليس بعدك شيء وأنت الظاهر فليس فوقك شيء وأنت الباطن فليس دونك شيء اقض عني الدين وأغنني عن الفقر". ورواه البخاري أيضا في التاريخ الكبير. - ورواه الترمذي في الجامع الصحيح عن أبي هريرة - رضي الله تعالى عنه - قال : " كان رسول الله يأمرنا إذا أخذ أحدنا مضجعه أن يقول اللهم رب السماوات ورب الأرضين وربنا ورب كل شيء وفالق الحب والنوى ومنزل التوراة والإنجيل والقرآن أعوذ بك من شر كل ذي شر أنت آخذ بناصيته أنت الأول فليس قبلك شيء وأنت الآخر فليس بعدك شيء والظاهر فليس فوقك شيء والباطن فليس دونك شيء اقض عني الدين وأغنني من الفقر" قال أبو عيسى هذا حديث حسن صحيح. ورواه الإمام البيهقي في السنن الكبرى عن أبي هريرة، وعن عائشة رضي الله عنهما. وللحديث بهذا اللفظ روايات أخرى.(س). (٢) وهذا الإجماع مستند على روايات وردت في وصف الله تعالى بلفظ القديم، منها ما أشرنا إليه سابقاً ما رواه أبو داود، قال حدثنا إسماعيل بن بشر بن منصور ثنا عبد الرحمن بن مهدي عن عبد الله بن المبارك عن حيوة بن شريح قال : " لقيت عقبة بن مسلم فقلت له بلغني أنك حدثت عن عبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص مع عن النبي لا اله الا أنه كان إذا دخل المسجد قال أعوذ بالله العظيم وبوجهه الكريم وسلطانه القديم من الشيطان الرجيم قال أقط. قلت نعم قال فإذا قال ذلك قال الشيطان حفظ مني سائر اليوم". وهذا قوي السند، لا ينزل عن رتبة الحسن بوجه، ويصلح للاعتماد عليه وفيه تصريح بوصف الله تعالى وسلطانه بلفظ "القديم". إذا عرفت ذلك فلا تغتر بما تراه في تعليقات ابن باز على قول الإمام الطحاوي معترضا عليه : "هذا اللفظ لم يرد في أسماء الله الحسنى كما نبه عليه الشارح رحمه الله وغيره، وإنما ذكره كثير من علماء الكلام ليثبتوا به وجوده قبل كل شيء، وأسماء الله توقيفية لا يجوز إثبات شيء منها إلا بالنص من الكتاب العزيز أو السنة الصحيحة "اهـ. يستنكر في كلامه هذا على الإمام الطحاوي، وكلامه باطل ، يقصد بالشارح ابن أبي العز الحنفي الذي خالف اعتقاد الأحناف، والتابع الوفي لابن تيمية، وشرحه هذا يمثل في كثير من المواضع مذهب المجسمة ! وقد تبين لك أن هذا اللفظ ورد في السنة الصحيحة، وقد قام إجماع الأمة على جواز استعماله في وصف الله تعالى، كما نقل هذا الإجماع الزبيدي في شرح الإحياء ولا يضر هذا الإجماع مخالفة بعض الحشوية لعدم الاعتداء بهم ولا بما استندوا إليه ، علماً بأنه قد ورد أيضاً نسبة هذا اللفظ في أحاديث أخر منها ما رواه ابن ماجه عن أبي هريرة، في عد الأسماء وفيه اسم القديم. ورواه الحاكم أيضا في مستدركه عنه أيضا وفيه اسم القديم. وقد بينا ذلك تفصيلاً في حاشيتنا على متن الإمام الطحاوي، ونقدنا فيه جميع ما ادعاه ابن باز وبينا بطلانه و اختلال أركانه ، فانظره. علماً أنه يجوز على التحقيق إطلاق وصف على الله تعالى وإن لم يرد ، فلِمَ لَمْ يعتبر ابن باز كلمة القديم من الأوصاف لا من الأسماء؟ فلا يلزمه الاعتراض على العلماء. ولكن هذا شأنهم دائما يتعنتون في إلصاق التهم بغيرهم.(س)
Al-Bukhari narrated this hadith in al-Adab al-Mufrad from Abu Hurayra: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, used to say when he went to his bed: O Allah, Lord of the heavens and the earth and Lord of everything, Cleaver of the grain and the date-stone, Revealer of the Torah, the Gospel and the Qur'an, I seek refuge in You from every evil whose forelock You hold; You are the First, so there is nothing before You; You are the Last, so there is nothing after You; You are the Manifest, so there is nothing above You; You are the Hidden, so there is nothing below You; relieve me of debt and enrich me from poverty.' Al-Bukhari also narrated it in al-Tarikh al-Kabir. And al-Tirmidhi narrated it in al-Jami' al-Sahih from Abu Hurayra: 'The Messenger of Allah used to command us when one of us took his bed to say: O Allah, Lord of the heavens and Lord of the earths, our Lord and Lord of everything, Cleaver of the grain and the date-stone, Revealer of the Torah, the Gospel and the Qur'an, I seek refuge in You from the evil of every evil being whose forelock You hold; You are the First, so there is nothing before You; You are the Last, so there is nothing after You; You are the Manifest, so there is nothing above You; You are the Hidden, so there is nothing below You; relieve me of debt and enrich me from poverty.' Abu 'Isa said: This hadith is hasan sahih. And Imam al-Bayhaqi narrated it in al-Sunan al-Kubra from Abu Hurayra and from 'A'isha, may Allah be pleased with them. The hadith has other narrations with this wording. (2) And this consensus is based on narrations that came describing Allah with the word 'al-Qadim', among which is what we pointed to previously, what Abu Dawud narrated: Isma'il ibn Bishr ibn Mansur told us, 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Mahdi told us from 'Abd Allah ibn al-Mubarak from Haywa ibn Shurayh said: 'I met 'Uqba ibn Muslim and said to him: It has reached me that you narrated from 'Abd Allah ibn 'Amr ibn al-'As from the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, that when he entered the mosque he said: I seek refuge in Allah the Great, and in His noble Face, and His eternal authority (sultanihi al-qadim) from the accursed Satan. He said: Is that so? I said: Yes. He said: If he says that, Satan says: He has been protected from me for the rest of the day.' And this is strong in chain, not falling below the rank of hasan in any way, and is suitable for reliance, and in it is an explicit description of Allah Most High and His authority with the word 'al-Qadim'. If you know that, then do not be deceived by what you see in Ibn Baz's comments on the statement of Imam al-Tahawi objecting: 'This word has not come in the beautiful names of Allah as the commentator pointed out, and others; rather it was mentioned by many of the theologians (kalam scholars) to establish thereby His existence before everything, and the names of Allah are tawqifiyya (only known by revelation); it is not permissible to affirm any of them except by text from the Noble Book or sound Sunnah.' He disapproves in this statement of his of Imam al-Tahawi, and his statement is false. By 'the commentator' he means Ibn Abi al-'Izz al-Hanafi, who contradicted the belief of the Hanafis and was a faithful follower of Ibn Taymiyya, and his commentary represents in many places the doctrine of the anthropomorphists! And it has become clear to you that this word has come in the sound Sunnah, and the community has established consensus on the permissibility of using it in describing Allah Most High, as al-Zabidi transmitted this consensus in his commentary on al-Ihya', and this consensus is not harmed by the opposition of some of the hashwiyya (ignorant traditionalists) because they are not taken into account, nor what they rely on. Know that this word has also been reported in other hadiths, including what Ibn Majah narrated from Abu Hurayra in the enumeration of the names, and it includes the name 'al-Qadim'. And al-Hakim also narrated it in his Mustadrak from him, and it includes the name 'al-Qadim'. And we have detailed that in our gloss on the text of Imam al-Tahawi, and we criticized therein all that Ibn Baz claimed and showed its falsehood and the weakness of its pillars, so refer to it. Know that in verification it is permissible to apply a description to Allah Most High even if it is not revealed, so why did Ibn Baz not consider the word 'al-Qadim' as one of the descriptions (awsaf) rather than the names? Thus, he is not obliged to object to the scholars. But this is their habit always: they are obstinate in attaching accusations to others.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a defense of using the term 'Qadim' (Eternal) as an attribute of Allah. It first provides extensive hadith evidence from al-Bukhari, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Bayhaqi showing that the Prophet used the words 'al-Awwal' and 'al-Akhir', and also that the phrase 'sultanihi al-qadim' (His eternal authority) appears in a sahih hadith from Abu Dawud. The author stresses that this hadith is strong (hasan) and explicitly describes Allah and His authority with the word 'al-Qadim'. He then warns the reader not to be misled by Ibn Baz's objection to Imam al-Tahawi's use of the word 'Qadim', where Ibn Baz claimed it is not among the revealed names. The author refutes Ibn Baz by pointing out that: (1) the word is found in authentic hadiths, (2) there is consensus (ijma') of the ummah on its permissibility, as transmitted by al-Zabidi, (3) even if it were not a name, it is permissible to describe Allah with attributes that are not explicitly named, and (4) Ibn Baz's reliance on the commentary of Ibn Abi al-'Izz (who followed Ibn Taymiyya) is flawed because that commentary contains anthropomorphism. The author concludes that Ibn Baz's objection is baseless and stems from obstinacy.

الآخر
الظاهر
الباطن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The attribute 'al-Awwal' is not mentioned in the prophetic hadith.
Correction: This passage demonstrates that the Prophet explicitly said 'You are the First' in an authentic supplication.

Checkpoint
Which attribute in the hadith directly indicates that Allah has no beginning?
A) al-Akhir
B) al-Awwal
C) al-Zahir
D) al-Batin

Key Takeaway
The hadith of the Prophet's bedtime supplication provides authentic evidence that Allah is described as 'al-Awwal', affirming His pre-eternity, which is the same concept as 'al-Qadim'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah is the First, with nothing before Him? How does this belief affect your view of things you hold as 'original' or 'first' in your life? Will you consciously remind yourself tonight as you go to bed that He is al-Awwal, and let that reshape your worries about what came before?
?
When you recite 'أنت الأول فليس قبلك شيء' in this du'a, what does that mean for your own past regrets or sins? Can you internalize that Allah precedes everything, and thus nothing in your past can compete with His mercy? Commit to reciting this supplication tonight with full presence.
?
If Allah is al-Awwal with nothing before Him, then your entire existence is secondary and dependent. Are you living as if something else holds priority over Allah in your heart? Identify one competing priority and resolve to remove it from its place of precedence.

Refuting Ibn Baz's Objection to the Attribute 'Qadim'
Refutes Ibn Baz's objection to the attribute 'Qadim' using hadith and consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the arguments that refute Ibn Baz's claim that 'al-Qadim' is not a valid attribute of Allah because it is not among the revealed names.

Core Idea
The term 'al-Qadim' is found in authentic hadiths and supported by scholarly consensus, making its use permissible.

This lesson addresses the objection raised by Ibn Baz against using the attribute 'Qadim' for Allah. The author presents a hadith from Abu Dawud that explicitly uses 'sultanihi al-qadim', and then argues that there is consensus on its permissibility. The lesson also critiques Ibn Baz's reliance on the commentary of Ibn Abi al-'Izz, which contains anthropomorphic tendencies.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith from Abu Dawud
Read the Arabic passage and translation of the narration that uses 'sultanihi al-qadim' (His eternal authority).
2
Understand the consensus argument
The author states that there is consensus (ijma') on the permissibility of describing Allah as 'Qadim', as transmitted by al-Zabidi.
3
Analyze the refutation of Ibn Baz
Examine the reasons given: the word is in the Sunnah, it is permissible to describe Allah even without a specific name, and Ibn Baz's source is unreliable.
4
Reflect on the broader implication
Consider that the dispute reflects a difference between the Ash'ari/sunni view and the anthropomorphist (hashwiyya) view.

روى هذا الحديث البخاري في الأدب المفرد عن أبي هريرة قال : " كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : إذا أوى إلى فراشه اللهم رب السماوات والأرض ورب كل شيء فالق الحب والنوى منزل التوراة والإنجيل والقرآن أعوذ بك من كل ذي شر أنت آخذ بناصيته أنت الأول فليس قبلك شيء وأنت الآخر فليس بعدك شيء وأنت الظاهر فليس فوقك شيء وأنت الباطن فليس دونك شيء اقض عني الدين وأغنني عن الفقر". ورواه البخاري أيضا في التاريخ الكبير. - ورواه الترمذي في الجامع الصحيح عن أبي هريرة - رضي الله تعالى عنه - قال : " كان رسول الله يأمرنا إذا أخذ أحدنا مضجعه أن يقول اللهم رب السماوات ورب الأرضين وربنا ورب كل شيء وفالق الحب والنوى ومنزل التوراة والإنجيل والقرآن أعوذ بك من شر كل ذي شر أنت آخذ بناصيته أنت الأول فليس قبلك شيء وأنت الآخر فليس بعدك شيء والظاهر فليس فوقك شيء والباطن فليس دونك شيء اقض عني الدين وأغنني من الفقر" قال أبو عيسى هذا حديث حسن صحيح. ورواه الإمام البيهقي في السنن الكبرى عن أبي هريرة، وعن عائشة رضي الله عنهما. وللحديث بهذا اللفظ روايات أخرى.(س). (٢) وهذا الإجماع مستند على روايات وردت في وصف الله تعالى بلفظ القديم، منها ما أشرنا إليه سابقاً ما رواه أبو داود، قال حدثنا إسماعيل بن بشر بن منصور ثنا عبد الرحمن بن مهدي عن عبد الله بن المبارك عن حيوة بن شريح قال : " لقيت عقبة بن مسلم فقلت له بلغني أنك حدثت عن عبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص مع عن النبي لا اله الا أنه كان إذا دخل المسجد قال أعوذ بالله العظيم وبوجهه الكريم وسلطانه القديم من الشيطان الرجيم قال أقط. قلت نعم قال فإذا قال ذلك قال الشيطان حفظ مني سائر اليوم". وهذا قوي السند، لا ينزل عن رتبة الحسن بوجه، ويصلح للاعتماد عليه وفيه تصريح بوصف الله تعالى وسلطانه بلفظ "القديم". إذا عرفت ذلك فلا تغتر بما تراه في تعليقات ابن باز على قول الإمام الطحاوي معترضا عليه : "هذا اللفظ لم يرد في أسماء الله الحسنى كما نبه عليه الشارح رحمه الله وغيره، وإنما ذكره كثير من علماء الكلام ليثبتوا به وجوده قبل كل شيء، وأسماء الله توقيفية لا يجوز إثبات شيء منها إلا بالنص من الكتاب العزيز أو السنة الصحيحة "اهـ. يستنكر في كلامه هذا على الإمام الطحاوي، وكلامه باطل ، يقصد بالشارح ابن أبي العز الحنفي الذي خالف اعتقاد الأحناف، والتابع الوفي لابن تيمية، وشرحه هذا يمثل في كثير من المواضع مذهب المجسمة ! وقد تبين لك أن هذا اللفظ ورد في السنة الصحيحة، وقد قام إجماع الأمة على جواز استعماله في وصف الله تعالى، كما نقل هذا الإجماع الزبيدي في شرح الإحياء ولا يضر هذا الإجماع مخالفة بعض الحشوية لعدم الاعتداء بهم ولا بما استندوا إليه ، علماً بأنه قد ورد أيضاً نسبة هذا اللفظ في أحاديث أخر منها ما رواه ابن ماجه عن أبي هريرة، في عد الأسماء وفيه اسم القديم. ورواه الحاكم أيضا في مستدركه عنه أيضا وفيه اسم القديم. وقد بينا ذلك تفصيلاً في حاشيتنا على متن الإمام الطحاوي، ونقدنا فيه جميع ما ادعاه ابن باز وبينا بطلانه و اختلال أركانه ، فانظره. علماً أنه يجوز على التحقيق إطلاق وصف على الله تعالى وإن لم يرد ، فلِمَ لَمْ يعتبر ابن باز كلمة القديم من الأوصاف لا من الأسماء؟ فلا يلزمه الاعتراض على العلماء. ولكن هذا شأنهم دائما يتعنتون في إلصاق التهم بغيرهم.(س)
Al-Bukhari narrated this hadith in al-Adab al-Mufrad from Abu Hurayra: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, used to say when he went to his bed: O Allah, Lord of the heavens and the earth and Lord of everything, Cleaver of the grain and the date-stone, Revealer of the Torah, the Gospel and the Qur'an, I seek refuge in You from every evil whose forelock You hold; You are the First, so there is nothing before You; You are the Last, so there is nothing after You; You are the Manifest, so there is nothing above You; You are the Hidden, so there is nothing below You; relieve me of debt and enrich me from poverty.' Al-Bukhari also narrated it in al-Tarikh al-Kabir. And al-Tirmidhi narrated it in al-Jami' al-Sahih from Abu Hurayra: 'The Messenger of Allah used to command us when one of us took his bed to say: O Allah, Lord of the heavens and Lord of the earths, our Lord and Lord of everything, Cleaver of the grain and the date-stone, Revealer of the Torah, the Gospel and the Qur'an, I seek refuge in You from the evil of every evil being whose forelock You hold; You are the First, so there is nothing before You; You are the Last, so there is nothing after You; You are the Manifest, so there is nothing above You; You are the Hidden, so there is nothing below You; relieve me of debt and enrich me from poverty.' Abu 'Isa said: This hadith is hasan sahih. And Imam al-Bayhaqi narrated it in al-Sunan al-Kubra from Abu Hurayra and from 'A'isha, may Allah be pleased with them. The hadith has other narrations with this wording. (2) And this consensus is based on narrations that came describing Allah with the word 'al-Qadim', among which is what we pointed to previously, what Abu Dawud narrated: Isma'il ibn Bishr ibn Mansur told us, 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Mahdi told us from 'Abd Allah ibn al-Mubarak from Haywa ibn Shurayh said: 'I met 'Uqba ibn Muslim and said to him: It has reached me that you narrated from 'Abd Allah ibn 'Amr ibn al-'As from the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, that when he entered the mosque he said: I seek refuge in Allah the Great, and in His noble Face, and His eternal authority (sultanihi al-qadim) from the accursed Satan. He said: Is that so? I said: Yes. He said: If he says that, Satan says: He has been protected from me for the rest of the day.' And this is strong in chain, not falling below the rank of hasan in any way, and is suitable for reliance, and in it is an explicit description of Allah Most High and His authority with the word 'al-Qadim'. If you know that, then do not be deceived by what you see in Ibn Baz's comments on the statement of Imam al-Tahawi objecting: 'This word has not come in the beautiful names of Allah as the commentator pointed out, and others; rather it was mentioned by many of the theologians (kalam scholars) to establish thereby His existence before everything, and the names of Allah are tawqifiyya (only known by revelation); it is not permissible to affirm any of them except by text from the Noble Book or sound Sunnah.' He disapproves in this statement of his of Imam al-Tahawi, and his statement is false. By 'the commentator' he means Ibn Abi al-'Izz al-Hanafi, who contradicted the belief of the Hanafis and was a faithful follower of Ibn Taymiyya, and his commentary represents in many places the doctrine of the anthropomorphists! And it has become clear to you that this word has come in the sound Sunnah, and the community has established consensus on the permissibility of using it in describing Allah Most High, as al-Zabidi transmitted this consensus in his commentary on al-Ihya', and this consensus is not harmed by the opposition of some of the hashwiyya (ignorant traditionalists) because they are not taken into account, nor what they rely on. Know that this word has also been reported in other hadiths, including what Ibn Majah narrated from Abu Hurayra in the enumeration of the names, and it includes the name 'al-Qadim'. And al-Hakim also narrated it in his Mustadrak from him, and it includes the name 'al-Qadim'. And we have detailed that in our gloss on the text of Imam al-Tahawi, and we criticized therein all that Ibn Baz claimed and showed its falsehood and the weakness of its pillars, so refer to it. Know that in verification it is permissible to apply a description to Allah Most High even if it is not revealed, so why did Ibn Baz not consider the word 'al-Qadim' as one of the descriptions (awsaf) rather than the names? Thus, he is not obliged to object to the scholars. But this is their habit always: they are obstinate in attaching accusations to others.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a defense of using the term 'Qadim' (Eternal) as an attribute of Allah. It first provides extensive hadith evidence from al-Bukhari, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Bayhaqi showing that the Prophet used the words 'al-Awwal' and 'al-Akhir', and also that the phrase 'sultanihi al-qadim' (His eternal authority) appears in a sahih hadith from Abu Dawud. The author stresses that this hadith is strong (hasan) and explicitly describes Allah and His authority with the word 'al-Qadim'. He then warns the reader not to be misled by Ibn Baz's objection to Imam al-Tahawi's use of the word 'Qadim', where Ibn Baz claimed it is not among the revealed names. The author refutes Ibn Baz by pointing out that: (1) the word is found in authentic hadiths, (2) there is consensus (ijma') of the ummah on its permissibility, as transmitted by al-Zabidi, (3) even if it were not a name, it is permissible to describe Allah with attributes that are not explicitly named, and (4) Ibn Baz's reliance on the commentary of Ibn Abi al-'Izz (who followed Ibn Taymiyya) is flawed because that commentary contains anthropomorphism. The author concludes that Ibn Baz's objection is baseless and stems from obstinacy.

Key Terms

إجماع
توقيفية
الحشوية

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'Qadim' is not found in the Sunnah and is only used by theologians.
Correction: This passage shows that it is found in an authentic hadith (Abu Dawud) and is supported by consensus.

Checkpoint
What is the main evidence the author uses to refute Ibn Baz?
A) A hadith with 'sultanihi al-qadim'
B) A verse from the Qur'an
C) Logical reasoning alone
D) The opinion of Imam al-Tahawi

Key Takeaway
The attribute 'al-Qadim' is firmly established in the Sunnah and supported by scholarly consensus, making Ibn Baz's objection unfounded.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When a beloved scholar you respect says something that seems contradicted by an authentic hadith, do you have the courage to follow the hadith over the scholar? What will you do the next time this happens, especially if it means going against a group you are part of?
?
The author uses strong language against Ibn Baz and his followers. Have you ever dismissed an opposing view by labeling its holders with derogatory terms like 'hashwiyya' or 'mujassima' without fairly engaging their evidence? How can you repent from this and commit to respectful debate?
?
This lesson shows that even a revered figure like Ibn Baz can be wrong. Are you willing to admit that you too might be wrong in some firmly held beliefs? What specific belief do you need to re-examine in light of the evidence, not just follow what you were taught?

Definition and Proof of Baqa' (Everlastingness)
Defines Baqa' as absence of subsequent non-existence and provides scriptural proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of Baqa' as the absence of subsequent non-existence and its scriptural proofs from the Qur'an and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Allah's existence has no end—He is the Last without termination.

This lesson defines the second divine attribute, Baqa' (everlastingness), and grounds it in revelation. You will see how the Qur'an and hadith establish that Allah's existence is eternal in the future, just as Qidam established it is eternal in the past. The lesson also clarifies that Allah's everlastingness is unlike the temporal continuation of creatures.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the passage once without analysis. Let the author's definitions and proofs settle in your mind.
Pay attention to the flow from definition to proof to distinction.
2
Identify the definition and proofs
Find the exact definition of Baqa' and the two proofs: one from the Qur'an (Surah al-Rahman 27) and one from the Sunnah (the hadith).
The verse 'And there will remain the Face of your Lord' is interpreted as referring to Allah's essence.
3
Distinguish divine Baqa' from contingent Baqa'
The passage explains that Allah's everlastingness is not temporal and does not involve succession, unlike the continued existence of creatures.
This distinction prevents misunderstanding Allah's attribute as similar to created permanence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثانية البقاء وحقيقة البقاء عبارة عن انتفاء العدم اللاحق للذات والصفات وهو أول بلا بداية وآخر بلا نهاية. والدليل على البقاء من الكتاب قوله تعالى ﴿ وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ﴾ [الرحمن : ۲۷]، أي ذاته، فإن الوجه في الآية بمعنى الذات. ومن السنة قوله : "اللهم أنت الآخر فليس بعدك شيء". (1) البقاء هو عدم الآخرية للوجود ، فمعنى الله باق لا آخر لوجوده ، أي ليس لوجوده انقضاء وانتهاء فهو سبحانه موجود لا يلحق العدم وجوده ، قال تعالى ﴿ هُوَ الْأَوَّلُ وَالْآخِرُ ﴾ أي إن الله سبحانه الأول قبل كل شيء بلا بداية والآخر بعد كل شيء بلا نهاية، فالأول في الآية يدل على القدم، والآخر يدل على البقاء وكلاهما يستلزم وجوب وجوده تعالى وما تقدم هو معنى البقاء بالنسبة إلى ذات الله وصفاته، وأما معناه بالنسبة إلى الحادث فهو استمرار الوجود مع جواز الحوق العدم. (غ). بقاء الحادث زماني، وبقاء القديم ليس زمانياً، أي بقاء الحادث إنما يكون على التَّقضي والاستمرار بخلاف بقاء الله تعالى لأنه لا يطرأ عليه حال بعد حال، إذ لا يجوز عليه التغير أصلاً. (س).
The second is everlastingness (al-baqa'). The reality of everlastingness is an expression of the absence of non-existence after the essence and attributes; He is the First without beginning and the Last without end. The proof of everlastingness from the Book is His saying: "And there will remain the Face of your Lord" (al-Rahman 27), meaning His essence, for 'face' in the verse means essence. And from the Sunnah is his saying: "O Allah, You are the Last, so there is nothing after You." (1) Everlastingness is the absence of otherness (akhiriyya) for existence; the meaning of 'Allah is ever-lasting' is that there is no end to His existence, i.e., His existence has no termination or conclusion; He is Exalted, existing, and non-existence does not affect His existence. He said: "He is the First and the Last" (al-Hadid 3), meaning that Allah is the First before everything without beginning, and the Last after everything without end. The 'First' in the verse indicates pre-existence (qidam), and the 'Last' indicates everlastingness (baqa'), and both necessitate the necessity of His existence. What preceded is the meaning of everlastingness in relation to Allah's essence and attributes. As for its meaning in relation to the contingent (al-hadith), it is the continuation of existence with the possibility of subsequent non-existence. The everlastingness of the contingent is temporal (zamani), while the everlastingness of the Pre-existent (al-qadim) is not temporal. That is, the everlastingness of the contingent is in terms of succession and continuation, unlike the everlastingness of Allah, because no state after state occurs to Him, as change is absolutely impossible for Him.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage defines the second attribute, Baqa' (everlastingness), as the negation of non-existence after the essence and attributes. It then provides scriptural proofs: the Qur'anic verse 'And there will remain the Face of your Lord' (al-Rahman 27) interpreting 'Face' as the essence, and the hadith 'O Allah, You are the Last, so there is nothing after You.' The footnote elaborates that Baqa' means no end to existence, and contrasts it with the concept of 'otherness' (akhiriyya). It also highlights that the verse 'He is the First and the Last' (al-Hadid 3) combines both Qidam and Baqa'. The author distinguishes between the Baqa' of Allah (essential, non-temporal) and the Baqa' of contingent beings (temporal, involving succession). For Allah, there is no change or succession of states.

Key Terms
البقاء
آخر
عدم الآخرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The belief that Allah's Baqa' is like the continued existence of creatures, involving temporal succession and the possibility of non-existence.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Allah's Baqa' is not temporal; it has no ending and involves no change or succession of states.

Checkpoint
What is the meaning of Baqa' (everlastingness) for Allah according to this passage?
A) His existence continues through time.
B) His existence has no end and is not subject to succession.
C) His existence is followed by non-existence.
D) His existence is like the permanence of contingent beings.

Key Takeaway
Allah's Baqa' means His existence has no end and is not subject to temporal succession, as proven by the Qur'an and Sunnah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah is the Last with nothing after Him, then every pursuit you chase after—wealth, status, relationships—will end. Why do you invest so heavily in what will perish while neglecting the One who never does? How can you reorder your priorities today to reflect this truth?
?
The passage distinguishes between Allah's everlastingness (no succession) and the contingent's everlastingness (temporal and successive). Your own existence is a string of moments—past, present, future. How does knowing that Allah's existence is beyond all such division change the way you experience time? Are you living as if you have endless tomorrows, ignoring that you are contingent and your time is limited?
?
The hadith says 'You are the Last, so there is nothing after You.' If nothing is after Allah, then nothing can outlast Him. What have you placed after Him in your heart—what do you consider more lasting or more important than His pleasure? How would you need to think, speak, and act to truly make Him the Last in your life?

The Second Attribute: al-Baqa (Eternal Existence)
Sanusi defines al-Baqa and provides proof from Quran and Sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the divine attribute al-Baqa (eternal existence), its definition, and the textual evidence from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Al-Baqa means God's essence and attributes can never cease to exist.

In this lesson, we explore the second divine attribute discussed by Imam Sanusi: al-Baqa, or eternal existence. After establishing that God exists without a beginning, we now consider that His existence has no end. This attribute is distinct from mere existence and is proven by revelation. Let's read the passage carefully to grasp its meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of the content.
Notice that the passage begins by naming the attribute, then defines it, and then provides evidence.
2
Understand the definition
Focus on the phrase 'negation of subsequent non-existence for the essence and attributes.' Reflect on what it means for God to have no end.
The definition also relates to the names al-Awwal and al-Akhir (the First and the Last).
3
Examine the textual proofs
Look at the Quranic verse (55:27) and the hadith provided. Understand how they demonstrate the attribute of al-Baqa.
The verse interprets 'face' as essence, and the hadith describes Allah as the Last.
4
Note the consensus and rational proof
Notice that the author mentions the consensus of the ummah and that a rational proof will come later.
This shows that the attribute is established both by revelation and reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثانية البقاء
وحقيقة البقاء عبارة عن انتفاء العدم اللاحق للذات والصفات وهو أول بلا بداية وآخر بلا نهاية.
والدليل على البقاء من الكتاب قوله تعالى ( وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ) أي ذاته، فإن الوجه في الآية بمعنى الذات. ومن السنة قوله : "اللهم أنت الآخر فليس بعدك شيء". وقد أجمعت الأمة على أن الله تعالى متصف بالبقاء. وأما برهان العقل فسيأتي.
The second: al-Baqa (eternal existence). The reality of al-Baqa is the negation of subsequent non-existence for the essence and attributes, and He is the First without beginning and the Last without end. The evidence for al-Baqa from the Book is His statement (And there will remain the Face of your Lord) – i.e., His essence, for 'face' in the verse means essence. And from the Sunnah is his saying: 'O Allah, You are the Last, there is nothing after You.' And the ummah has unanimously agreed that Allah, exalted, is described with al-Baqa. As for the rational proof, it will come later.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage defines the second divine attribute, al-Baqa (eternal existence). It begins by giving its definition: it is the negation of non-existence that could occur after the essence and attributes. It emphasizes that God is the First without beginning and the Last without end. Then it provides textual evidence: from the Quran, the verse 'And there will remain the Face of your Lord' (55:27), where 'face' is interpreted as the essence; and from the Sunnah, the hadith 'O Allah, You are the Last, there is nothing after You.' It then states the consensus of the Muslim community on this attribute and notes that the rational proof will follow later.

Key Terms
البقاء
العدم
الذات
الصفات
الأول
الآخر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that al-Baqa is the same as the attribute of existence.
Correction: Al-Baqa is a distinct attribute that specifically negates the possibility of annihilation, whereas the attribute of existence simply affirms that God exists.

Checkpoint
What is the definition of al-Baqa according to this passage?
A) It is the attribute of existence without beginning.
B) It is the negation of subsequent non-existence for the essence and attributes.
C) It is the attribute of being the First and Last.
D) It is the name of a place in the afterlife.

Key Takeaway
Al-Baqa is the attribute that Allah will never cease to exist, and it is proven by revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that Allah is 'the Last, there is nothing after Him,' would you fear losing anything other than Him? What would change in your priorities today?
?
The attribute of al-Baqa means Allah will never cease to exist. Everything you love in this world will end. Does your heart cling to the Eternal One as it should? What step will you take today to attach yourself more to Him?
?
You are reading about an attribute that most do not ponder deeply. After this lesson, you cannot claim ignorance. How will you live differently knowing that Allah alone remains? Write one concrete action you will take before the day ends.

Evidence for 'al-Qadim' in Sunnah and Consensus
Author presents hadith evidence and consensus for 'al-Qadim' as a divine term.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the term 'al-Qadim' is established in authentic hadith and supported by consensus of the ummah, refuting Ibn Baz's objection.

Core Idea
'Al-Qadim' is a legitimate description of Allah, proven by hadith and consensus.

In this passage, the editor responds to Ibn Baz's claim that 'al-Qadim' is not among Allah's names. He first establishes the strong chain of a hadith that explicitly uses this term, then cites additional narrations from Ibn Majah and al-Hakim. He further argues that the ummah has consensus on its permissibility, as reported by al-Zabidi.

Guided Path
1
Read the beginning of the passage
Read the Arabic from 'وهذا قوي السند' to 'فانظره' along with the translation. Note how the author first establishes the hadith's authenticity.
2
Identify the hadith evidence
Locate the mention of the hadith from Abu Hurayra and the narrations of Ibn Majah and al-Hakim. Understand that the author considers this sufficient proof.
The author also mentions his own detailed critique elsewhere.
3
Understand the consensus argument
Notice the claim that the ummah has consensus, and that opposition from the Hashwiyya does not harm it. This strengthens the case.
4
Reflect on Ibn Baz's objection
Consider why the author calls Ibn Baz's statement false and points out his reliance on Ibn Abi al-Izz.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا قوي السند، لا ينزل عن رتبة الحسن بوجه، ويصلح للاعتماد عليه وفيه تصريح بوصف الله تعالى وسلطانه بلفظ "القديم". إذا عرفت ذلك فلا تغتر بما تراه في تعليقات ابن باز على قول الإمام الطحاوي معترضا عليه : "هذا اللفظ لم يرد في أسماء الله الحسنى كما نبه عليه الشارح رحمه الله وغيره، وإنما ذكره كثير من علماء الكلام ليثبتوا به وجوده قبل كل شيء، وأسماء الله توقيفية لا يجوز إثبات شيء منها إلا بالنص من الكتاب العزيز أو السنة الصحيحة "اهـ. يستنكر في كلامه هذا على الإمام الطحاوي، وكلامه باطل ، يقصد بالشارح ابن أبي العز الحنفي الذي خالف اعتقاد الأحناف، والتابع الوفي لابن تيمية، وشرحه هذا يمثل في كثير من المواضع مذهب المجسمة ! وقد تبين لك أن هذا اللفظ ورد في السنة الصحيحة، وقد قام إجماع الأمة على جواز استعماله في وصف الله تعالى، كما نقل هذا الإجماع الزبيدي في شرح الإحياء ولا يضر هذا الإجماع مخالفة بعض الحشوية لعدم الاعتداء بهم ولا بما استندوا إليه ، علماً بأنه قد ورد أيضاً نسبة هذا اللفظ في أحاديث أخر منها ما رواه ابن ماجه عن أبي هريرة، في عد الأسماء وفيه اسم القديم. ورواه الحاكم أيضا في مستدركه عنه أيضا وفيه اسم القديم. وقد بينا ذلك تفصيلاً في حاشيتنا على متن الإمام الطحاوي، ونقدنا فيه جميع ما ادعاه ابن باز وبينا بطلانه و اختلال أركانه ، فانظره. علماً أنه يجوز على التحقيق إطلاق وصف على الله تعالى وإن لم يرد ، فلِمَ لَمْ يعتبر ابن باز كلمة القديم من الأوصاف لا من الأسماء؟ فلا يلزمه الاعتراض على العلماء. ولكن هذا شأنهم دائما يتعنتون في إلصاق التهم بغيرهم.
And this has a strong chain, not below the rank of good (hasan) in any way, and is suitable for reliance, and in it is an explicit description of God, exalted, and His authority with the term 'al-Qadim'. If you have understood that, then do not be deceived by what you see in the comments of Ibn Baz on the statement of Imam al-Tahawi, objecting to him: 'This term has not been reported among the beautiful names of God, as the commentator (rahimahullah) and others have noted; rather, it was mentioned by many theologians (kalam scholars) to establish His existence before everything, and the names of God are tawqifiyya (based on revelation); it is not permissible to establish any of them except by a text from the Noble Book or the authentic Sunnah.' He (Ibn Baz) disapproves in this statement of his of Imam al-Tahawi, and his statement is false. He meant by 'the commentator' Ibn Abi al-Izz al-Hanafi, who contradicted the creed of the Hanafis, and was a loyal follower of Ibn Taymiyya, and his commentary represents in many places the doctrine of the anthropomorphists (mujassima)! And it has become clear to you that this term is reported in the authentic Sunnah, and there is a consensus of the ummah on the permissibility of using it in describing God, as al-Zabidi transmitted this consensus in his commentary on al-Ihya'. And this consensus is not harmed by the opposition of some of the Hashwiyya (crude literalists), for they are not reckoned and what they rely on is not counted. Moreover, this term has also been reported in other hadiths, including what Ibn Majah narrated from Abu Hurayra in the enumeration of the names, and in it is the name 'al-Qadim'. Al-Hakim also narrated it in his Mustadrak from him as well, and in it is the name 'al-Qadim'. And we have detailed that in our commentary on the text of Imam al-Tahawi, and we have criticized all that Ibn Baz claimed and demonstrated its falsehood and the weakness of its foundations, so look at it. Know that it is permissible, according to verified research, to apply a description to God even if it is not reported, so why did Ibn Baz not consider the word 'al-Qadim' as a description rather than a name? Thus his objection to the scholars is not necessary. But this is always their way: they are obstinate in attaching accusations to others.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This is an editorial footnote defending the use of the term 'al-Qadim' to describe God, against Ibn Baz's objection that it is not one of the revealed names. The author argues that the term is supported by an authentic hadith with a strong chain, and that there is a consensus of the ummah on its permissibility, as reported by al-Zabidi. He also points out that Ibn Baz's criticism is directed at Imam al-Tahawi, and that the commentator Ibn Abi al-Izz, whom Ibn Baz relies on, represents the anthropomorphist (mujassima) school. The author provides additional hadith evidence from Ibn Majah and al-Hakim. He further argues that even if it were not a name, it is permissible to use it as a description. He concludes by accusing Ibn Baz and his ilk of obstinate accusation-mongering.

Key Terms
القديم
ابن باز
ابن أبي العز
المجسمة
الحشوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'al-Qadim' is not a legitimate term for Allah because it is not in the Quran or authentic hadith.
Correction: The author shows it is in authentic hadith and supported by consensus.

Checkpoint
Why does the author consider Ibn Baz's objection false?
A) Because Ibn Baz relied on weak hadiths.
B) Because the term is in the Quran.
C) Because the term is supported by authentic hadith and consensus.
D) Because Ibn Baz was not a scholar.

Key Takeaway
The term 'al-Qadim' is authentically reported in hadith and there is a consensus on its use as a description of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a critique of a theological term like 'al-Qadim', do you automatically side with a well-known scholar (e.g., Ibn Baz) without verifying the primary sources? How can you cultivate the habit of going back to the Quran and Sunnah yourself?
?
The author dismisses the opposition of 'al-Hashwiyya' as insignificant. Is there a group or opinion you have casually dismissed without understanding their evidence? What would it take for you to fairly evaluate views you disagree with?
?
Consensus (ijma') is presented as decisive evidence. Are you part of a community that upholds the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah, or have you isolated yourself with a minority view? What one step can you take today to align your theology with the mainstream Sunni tradition?
